  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_ea7446d4-6b28-4498-b8c5-4e761f4d038e'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer14267110335334976185"><b>Lara Jean is having <i>the best</i> senior year.</b><br/><br/>And there’s still so much to look forward to: a class trip to New York City, prom with her boyfriend Peter, Beach Week after graduation, and her dad’s wedding to Ms. Rothschild. Then she’ll be off to college with Peter, at a school close enough for her to come home and bake chocolate chip cookies on the weekends.<br/><br/>Life couldn’t be mor</span>
  <span id="freeText14267110335334976185" style="display:none"><b>Lara Jean is having <i>the best</i> senior year.</b><br /><br />And there’s still so much to look forward to: a class trip to New York City, prom with her boyfriend Peter, Beach Week after graduation, and her dad’s wedding to Ms. Rothschild. Then she’ll be off to college with Peter, at a school close enough for her to come home and bake chocolate chip cookies on the weekends.<br /><br />Life couldn’t be more perfect!<br /><br />At least, that’s what Lara Jean thinks . . . until she gets some unexpected news.<br /><br />Now the girl who dreads change must rethink all her plans—but when your heart and your head are saying two different things, which one should you listen to?</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637293025?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637293025" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9827205723021306167"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494471821i/22718041._SX540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>❝One day all of this will be proof, proof that we were here, proof that we loved each other. It’s the guarantee that no matter what happens to us in the future, this time was ours.❞</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>After delaying my reading for as long as I possibly could when it comes to Jenny's books, I am finally bringing Lara Jean's story to a close. For sure this time lol. And I must say, my heart truly aches. Peter Kavinsky, Lara Jean, the Song/Covey family, and just these books in general are so near and dear </span>
  <span id="freeText9827205723021306167" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494471821i/22718041._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>❝One day all of this will be proof, proof that we were here, proof that we loved each other. It’s the guarantee that no matter what happens to us in the future, this time was ours.❞</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>After delaying my reading for as long as I possibly could when it comes to Jenny's books, I am finally bringing Lara Jean's story to a close. For sure this time lol. And I must say, my heart truly aches. Peter Kavinsky, Lara Jean, the Song/Covey family, and just these books in general are so near and dear to my heart. I never knew how much this trilogy meant to me until now when I know it's finally goodbye. 😢<br><br>I can't even begin to explain just how eerily similar my life is to that of Lara Jean's and her family. We're Asian. My family consists of three girls like Margot, Lara Jean, and Kitty. Our mother passed away a few years ago. It's just me, my sisters, and my dad. My dad is finally dating again and is slowly moving on. My first and only relationship to this day all started in high school. I like to think that my boyfriend is the Peter K to my Lara Jean because five years later we're still going strong after high school and even in college. Although in my case, I am the oldest and I should probably be the Margot in the family, I can't help but think that I am the Lara Jean to my own story. THESE BOOKS ARE MY LIFE.<br><br>I wish I could say more but these books truly speak for themselves. I am so grateful for the journey that Jenny Han took us on for the past few years and Lara Jean, Peter K, and the Song girls will always be a part of me in such a unique way. Although it seems like the end of Lara Jean's story, in truth, it is only just the beginning of a whole new chapter of her life. After all, they say that every story has an end but in life, every ending is just a new beginning.<br><br>Thank you for all the laughs, tears, chocolate chip cookies, and memories. ❤️<br><br>Always and forever,<br>Mikee Andrea<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1494471821i/22718042._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>

<div id="review_2237462373" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2237462373" />
    <a title="Emma Giordano" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano"><img alt="Emma Giordano" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1569693958p2/30604861.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2237462373?book_show_action=true">Jan 09, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emma Giordano" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emma Giordano" href="/user/show/30604861-emma-giordano">Emma Giordano</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/30604861-emma-giordano?shelf=audiobooks">audiobooks</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2237462373" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1736328734372985686">4.5 Stars! Really enjoyed this conclusion! Definitely an improvement from book 2 in my opinion.<br/> <br/>I believe <i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is the most mature and well-developed of the TATBILB series. It successfully tackles real-teen issues while remaining entertaining and loveable.<br/><br/>As always, my favorite bits of these books are the family dynamics. In addition to the ever-wonderful sister dynamics, I enjoyed a fresh bit of conflict between such a close-knit family. It was well-written and expertly </span>
  <span id="freeText1736328734372985686" style="display:none">4.5 Stars! Really enjoyed this conclusion! Definitely an improvement from book 2 in my opinion.<br /> <br />I believe <i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is the most mature and well-developed of the TATBILB series. It successfully tackles real-teen issues while remaining entertaining and loveable.<br /><br />As always, my favorite bits of these books are the family dynamics. In addition to the ever-wonderful sister dynamics, I enjoyed a fresh bit of conflict between such a close-knit family. It was well-written and expertly executed. Also, I REALLY enjoyed seeing Kitty grow into her own person – her development was something I didn’t realize I desired until it was included.<br /><br />I also very much enjoyed the college talk in this book. For some reason, I feel many YA novels either take place before college is a concern, or else the conversation is omitted for “more entertaining plot points.” I found Lara Jean’s struggle with debating between colleges, coping with rejection, and finding the balance between her life at home and her life away at college to be one of the best portrayals of this time in a teen’s life that I’ve ever read. Though I never personally experienced any large bumps in my pre-college journey or can relate to the difficulty in deciding to go away for school, I feel this book is genuine and authentic in expressing an obstacle many high school students face.<br /><br />Additionally, I was so happy the relationship troubles of book 1 and 2 appeared to be absent, leaving room for more mature, realistic dating troubles to ensue. This book adds a layer of maturity the story, especially regarding relationships. I did not feel as frustrated with the romance as I have in the previous books because the characters were dealing with realistic and understandable conflicts and resolved them in satisfying ways.<br /><br />I don't have many critiques for this novel. I will say, I found the entire book predictable, there isn't a surprise or a twist that I did not guess beforehand, but that did not take away from my enjoyment of the story. I've really enjoyed diving back into the life of Lara Jean and would definitely recommend this series to my followers (especially the audiobooks!)</span>
  <a data-text-id="1736328734372985686" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1637188789?book_show_action=true">May 13, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kai" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kai" href="/user/show/41788524-kai">Kai</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/41788524-kai?shelf=finished-series">finished-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1637188789" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15674545682479747699"><i>"Never say no when you really want to say yes."</i><br/><br/><i>To All the Boys I've Loved Before</i> is a very light and simple trilogy. I don't think I really needed to read it - I don't think I would have missed out on anything - but it was fun anyway. And sometimes a lighthearted and gentle read is all you really need.<br/><br/>Compared to the other books in the series, <i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is my least favourite one. First of all, because it is missing a plot. Here and there were some exciting moments, but no rea</span>
  <span id="freeText15674545682479747699" style="display:none"><i>"Never say no when you really want to say yes."</i><br /><br /><i>To All the Boys I've Loved Before</i> is a very light and simple trilogy. I don't think I really needed to read it - I don't think I would have missed out on anything - but it was fun anyway. And sometimes a lighthearted and gentle read is all you really need.<br /><br />Compared to the other books in the series, <i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is my least favourite one. First of all, because it is missing a plot. Here and there were some exciting moments, but no real thread. Lara Jean bakes lots of cookies, does some crafting and hangs out with her boyfriend and her little sister.<br />(By the way: which 11-year-old girl has seen the DiCaprio Romeo and Juliet movie a bazillion times and loves it?)<br />Anyway, I just missed the action.<br />The second thing that really bothered me is a big spoiler. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I was rooting for John Ambrose McClaren. He was the reason Jenny Han wrote Book 2! And the way Peter treated Lara Jean in PSISLY annoyed me a lot. I was sure that book 3 was written so he and Lara would break up, and Lara would get together with John. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> I hope, one day, this dream will come true. But as I believe that this is the final book in the series, it will most likely only happen in my head.<br /><br />I'm not sure how to rate this. It wasn't a three-star read, but two stars seems a bit harsh. I'll go with three for now, but I might change my rating later.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.instagram.com/kaispellmeier/" rel="nofollow noopener">Find more of my books on Instagram</a></span>

          </span>

<div id="review_2503057646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2503057646" />
    <a title="Maria" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/77602709-maria"><img alt="Maria" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1519184646p2/77602709.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2503057646?book_show_action=true">Aug 24, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria" href="/user/show/77602709-maria">Maria</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2503057646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18066325109516211022"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br/><br/><blockquote>“Never say no when you really want to say yes.” </blockquote><br/><br/>This was such a weak ending to a trilogy. As I said in my previous review, this book shouldn't exist. This series could easily be a duology and it would be a strong one. The last two books had nothing to offer plot-wise. Especially this one. This book entailed <b>NO PLOT</b>. I swear to God! <b>NOTHING HAPPENED IN THIS BOOK</b>. 325 pages of cutsy moments, mommy and daddy, domestic life and food! Ugh the food! It was more present than ever in t</span>
  <span id="freeText18066325109516211022" style="display:none"><b>3</b>/5 Stars ⭐️ ⭐️ ⭐️<br /><br /><blockquote>“Never say no when you really want to say yes.” </blockquote><br /><br />This was such a weak ending to a trilogy. As I said in my previous review, this book shouldn't exist. This series could easily be a duology and it would be a strong one. The last two books had nothing to offer plot-wise. Especially this one. This book entailed <b>NO PLOT</b>. I swear to God! <b>NOTHING HAPPENED IN THIS BOOK</b>. 325 pages of cutsy moments, mommy and daddy, domestic life and food! Ugh the food! It was more present than ever in this book. Anyway, let's go.<br /><br /><i>Lara Jean is having the best senior year. And there’s still so much to look forward to: a class trip to New York City, prom with her boyfriend Peter, Beach Week after graduation, and her dad’s wedding to Ms. Rothschild. Then she’ll be off to college with Peter, at a school close enough for her to come home and bake chocolate chip cookies on the weekends.<br /><br />Life couldn’t be more perfect!<br /><br />At least, that’s what Lara Jean thinks…until she gets some unexpected news.<br /><br />Now the girl who dreads change must rethink all her plans—but when your heart and your head are saying two different things, which one should you listen to?</i><br /><br />This book contained no conflict. Gen is not present, Josh is away with his new girlfriend, all the sisters are doing well together, their father has a new wife, there is no love triangle or any other option for Lara Jean, John is nowhere to be found. This book felt like a novella to me, of how things are with Peter and Lara Jean and her family. Like??? ??? I was waiting for something <b>ANYTHING</b> to happen and nothing. I was certain John or Josh would come back and shake the waters a bit but nothing. Peter and Lara Jean is the main couple. This book defied the purpose of this entire trilogy. <br /><br />The only interesting part of this book, was the conflict with which university Lara Jean would choose. This was honestly the only thing that happened in this book, regarding the plot. I was so certain we would see Lara Jean's life at college and how she would cope without Peter <i>*gag*</i> but the book was too busy wasting 325 pages on domestic life. UGH. I'm glad the book chose the direction of Lara Jean picking her future over a boy... it showed some maturity on her part. Took her long enough, though. And she's still with the boy, but you know, semantics. <br /><br />I don't understand something. Is life in America so perfect? Do they all do these things for each other, is everything so extravagant? Because the entire other world is working differently. I swear, throughout this whole series my eyes ware rolling so hard. Their lives just seemed so damn perfect, I wanted to punch myself. Like??? ??? You know what I mean. I was jealous of their little circle and all the nice shit they did for each other, and their amazing childhood and everything! Just <b>SHUT UP! LIFE IS NOT LIKE THIS! </b><br /><br />I... don't know what else to say. These books kept me company for three days and I'm grateful for that. They were fun and cute. Problematic and cringy, at times, but I'm 21 years old. I can't see these kinds of book anymore otherwise. I didn't particularly enjoy the direction these books took, it was interesting how she author didn't follow the whole triangle in every book aspect but she didn't succeed. She just lowered the interest of the books. I can't wait for the next movie, I hope they add some exciting elements to it. Because, honestly, this book just lacked everything. It existed just to exist. Anyway, till the next one, K BYE!</span>
  <a data-text-id="18066325109516211022" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">maybe if you are 14 or if you are new to reading YA</span></div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer1764146850" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer2268490156077552638"><i> 2.25/5 stars <br/><br/><blockquote> <b> Don't be the girl who goes to college with a boyfriend. </b>
</blockquote></i>  <br/>I must have read an entirely different series than everyone else. <br/> <br/>I must have. It’s the only reasonable explanation.<br/> <br/>I always see reviews stating that these books are so cute and relatable? They leave me befuddled because I find them to be neither. Cute? No. Relatable? No. Annoying? Yes. Unnecessary? Yes. <br/> <br/><i> Me, when this book was over: </i><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496716407ra/22945325.gif' width='500' height='249' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><s> Why did I even pick this up? Curse you adorable covers. I have always known you were </s></span>
  <span id="freeText2268490156077552638" style="display:none"><i> 2.25/5 stars <br><br><blockquote> <b> Don't be the girl who goes to college with a boyfriend. </b>
</blockquote></i>  <br>I must have read an entirely different series than everyone else. <br> <br>I must have. It’s the only reasonable explanation.<br> <br>I always see reviews stating that these books are so cute and relatable? They leave me befuddled because I find them to be neither. Cute? No. Relatable? No. Annoying? Yes. Unnecessary? Yes. <br> <br><i> Me, when this book was over: </i><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496716407ra/22945325.gif" width="500" height="249" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><s> Why did I even pick this up? Curse you adorable covers. I have always known you were my kryptonite </s><br> <br>Luckily, I buddy read this with the amazing <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/show/418203" rel="nofollow noopener">Scrill!!!!!! </a> who, somehow, read the same book that I did and had similar thoughts and feelings. Thanks Scrill. I’m glad you didn’t leave me alone in this. <br><br><b> What I wanted to happen in this book: </b><br>1. Lara Jean to grow up and start acting her age. <br><br><b> What didn't happen in this book: </b><br>1. Lara Jean growing up and acting her age. <br><br>How old was she even suppose to be? Because I'm not buying this 17/18 year old thing. She's passable at twelve. <br><br>Was I suppose to like Lara Jean? I literally couldn't care less about anything that happened to her. She's just so immature and naive for her age. It would be one thing if she started out like that in the beginning of the series and did an entire 360 and was this strong, independent women at the end. But she wasn't, of course. She was still naive Lara Jean, the most consistent character I have had to read about. Every time she had any piece of dialogue, my eyes rolled so far to the back of my head that they might as well bought a vacation house there. <br><br><s> I wish I tagged this book as I read so I'd have more receipts. #regerts </s><br><br><blockquote> <i> I think couples costumes might be my favorite part of being in a couple. Besides the kissing, and the free rides, and Peter himself. </i>
</blockquote>  <br>What about the being with someone who fully understands you and who you are able to connect with? Who will support you and be with you no matter what? There's more to a relationship then couple costumes, kissing, and free rides. Or is that too much to ask for from a twelve-year-old? <br><br>Also, in case you were wondering what Lara Jean's day is like. Step-by-step. Not even the littlest of details missing, then this is the book for you. Because she will tell you everything that happens to her. Important to the story or not. Usually the latter. <br><br><blockquote> <i> I'm the cook. When we first got to the house, we went and did a big shopping trip and bought cold cuts, granola, dried pasta and jars of sauce, salsa, cereal. The one thing we didn't buy was toilet paper, which we ran out of on the second day. Every time we leave the house to eat lunch or dinner out, one of us steals a wad of toilet paper from the restaurant bathroom. Why we don't just go buy more, I don't know, but it turned into kind of a game. Chris is the clear winner, because she managed to get an economy-sized roll out of the dispenser, and she smuggled it out under her shirt. </i>
</blockquote> <br>Like I guess that's supposed to be funny? But after almost 300 pages of unnecessary detail, the last thing I possibly care about was if Lara Jean had toilet paper or not. I didn't care. I still don't care. <br><br>Also, was I suppose to care about LJ and Peter's relationship? Was I suppose to root for them to stay together? <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ Because the only salvageable part of this entire book was towards the end and they predictably broke up. When that happened I was pretty much like<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496716221ra/22945290.gif" width="500" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> <br><br>If you are a fan of classic movies, much like I am, then you'll remember in one of the most iconic musical of all time, <i> High School Musical 3 </i>, when Gabriella broke up with Troy's sorry ass because she realized that her education at Stanford was more important than any relationship. <a href="https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=fWRgXDsfEw4" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <s> If you don't remember, here's a link to the heartbreaking, but totally realistic scene </s>
</a> Someone please have a movie marathon with Lara Jean and show her that entire movie like three times. She really needs to see it and learn that PETER IS NOT MORE IMPORTANT THAN GETTING A GOOD EDUCATION. <br><br>Honestly this entire book I was just hoping Lara Jean would pull a Gabriella and dump Peter and go live her life boyfriend-free. Just walk away, girl. You deserve better than that asshole. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1496715015ra/22945074.gif" width="500" height="274" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Honestly, Lara Jean and Peter have nothing in common at all. <s> Unlike Troy and Gabriella, who were both insanely attractive people who could sing like angels </s>. What did they even talk about? None of the conversations they ever had in this book were ever actually meaningful. <br><br>Then there's Kitty who so impossibly annoying. She's what eleven? I don't think she's ever been told her entire life the word "no." There are scenes where she's up past midnight and no one even gets mad at her. Or she says the meanest things ever and barely gets a negative reaction. Then she's told she can't come to a bachelorette party BECAUSE SHE'S ELEVEN so she sneaks her way into the bachelor party. Just no Kitty. Go back to playing with your dog <s> who's non-existent this entire book </s>.<br><br>I would talk about how ridiculous the plot of this book is except there is no plot. <br><br>None. <br><br>At all.<br><br>Everytime a conflict comes up it gets solved by the next page. <br><br>Literally I fell asleep reading this book about 7 times and that's not an exaggeration. <br><br>I mean if you like this book. That's cool. I'm glad you did. But I'm gonna go back to reading <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/3351454.Morgan_Matson" title="Morgan Matson" rel="nofollow noopener">Morgan Matson</a> contemporary books. I think I'm done with Jenny Han. She just isn't for me. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449017000ra/17221417.gif" width="500" height="273" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_1638673585" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1638673585" />
    <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga"><img alt="Beatrice Masaluñga" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603719912p2/4590441.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1638673585?book_show_action=true">May 15, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Beatrice Masaluñga" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Beatrice Masaluñga" href="/user/show/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga">Beatrice Masaluñga</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">EVERYONE</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=owned">owned</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=signed-copy">signed-copy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4590441-beatrice-masalu-ga?shelf=favorite-books">favorite-books</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638673585" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2919884114629179854">What I feel like <u>before</u>, <u>during</u>, and <u>after</u> reading this book:<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488495214ra/22123138.gif' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is <b>a marvelous conclusion to this trilogy.</b> I'm not convinced Lara Jean and Peter K.'s story ends in a duology. When Jenny Han announced there will be a third and final book, I'm so delighted because my prayer to book gods for a one last hurrah has been answered and my waiting game is WORTH IT! Another bet is on for whose ship is going to sail and guys, I'm glad to say <b>MY SHIP SAILS! OMG! MY. SHIP. FUDGING.</b></span>
  <span id="freeText2919884114629179854" style="display:none">What I feel like <u>before</u>, <u>during</u>, and <u>after</u> reading this book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1488495214ra/22123138.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><i>Always and Forever, Lara Jean</i> is <b>a marvelous conclusion to this trilogy.</b> I'm not convinced Lara Jean and Peter K.'s story ends in a duology. When Jenny Han announced there will be a third and final book, I'm so delighted because my prayer to book gods for a one last hurrah has been answered and my waiting game is WORTH IT! Another bet is on for whose ship is going to sail and guys, I'm glad to say <b>MY SHIP SAILS! OMG! MY. SHIP. FUDGING. SAILS. TO. FOREVER. AND. EVER! OMG I LOVE YOU JENNY HAN! YOU ARE THE BEST! </b> <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <b>LJS + PK = FOREVER YAAASSSS!</b>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1493880107ra/22661705.gif" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I'm so FREAKING happy that my heart can't even calm down right now and the ending is simply beautiful it brought me tears of joy. I'm fangirling so hard right now OMG SOMEONE HOLD ME! I have so much love for this book. <b>The romance is so heartwarming, sweet, adorable and cute.</b> It has a lot of good vibes and moments that will make you giddy. I enjoyed every moment of it. <br><br>Aside from that, <b> I love how the story centers about adjustment to changes </b>. As the time flies by, changes are inevitable and sometimes, not everything is in our favor. Lara Jean makes out the best of her Senior Year High School with her boyfriend. They'll go together in the same college near home as planned. Everything is organized until she received her acceptance letter that makes her think laying out a new plan. She's still the goody-two shoes Lara Jean but she has a great character development in this book. She's more confident, flexible and welcoming to new options. Kudos to the Covey family for having a strong bond, to Ms. Rothschild who made the Covey household livelier and to Kitty Song Covey (my favorite Song sister) who's forever witty and funny. <br><br>Someday, I'll reread this trilogy and swoon over it again. I'm going to miss all the characters and I'm incredibly satisfied with the ending. If you haven't started this trilogy, I highly recommend it. <b>Thank you very much Jenny Han for sharing their story to us and making them part of our lives...forever.</b> <br><br> Here's my pre-review for this book. I put a spoiler tag to make it spoiler free. <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[SEPT 22 2016: THE GORGEOUS COVER = COVERGASM<br><br>MY ANSWERED PRAYER. <br><br>FINALLY. <br><br>MORE LARA JEAN AND PETER KAVINSKY. <br><br>LET THIS SHIP SAIL TO FOREVER.<br><br>GIVE JOHN AMBROSE MCCLAREN A NEW LOVE LIFE. [I LOVE YOU BUT STAY AWAY FROM MY SHIP]<br><br>LOVE YOU JENNY HAN BUT DON'T RUIN THIS! HAHAHA!  <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_2360240540" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2360240540" />
    <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court"><img alt="High Lady of The Night Court" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1556501727p2/62560505.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2360240540?book_show_action=true">Apr 13, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="High Lady of The Night Court" class="user" itemprop="url" name="High Lady of The Night Court" href="/user/show/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court">High Lady of The Night Court</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/62560505-high-lady-of-the-night-court?shelf=contemporary-read">contemporary-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2360240540" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3559276260006672790">Jenny Han your writing is creepily brilliant, I know these books will stick with me. All three of them feel evergreen, they will last in my heart forever. I had the best time reading this trilogy and as always am inevitably sad to have seen this book end.<br/>I understand Lara Jean’s concept of writing the letters. I don’t think they remove her feelings for the boys but sorts her feelings out. I think all of do this in some way or another, the best example to prove it is that we all feel free of the </span>
  <span id="freeText3559276260006672790" style="display:none">Jenny Han your writing is creepily brilliant, I know these books will stick with me. All three of them feel evergreen, they will last in my heart forever. I had the best time reading this trilogy and as always am inevitably sad to have seen this book end.<br />I understand Lara Jean’s concept of writing the letters. I don’t think they remove her feelings for the boys but sorts her feelings out. I think all of do this in some way or another, the best example to prove it is that we all feel free of the need to scream after reading a great book, once we’ve either reviewed it or ranted about it with someone who understands. It helps us get our emotions in order and it absorbs all those overwhelming feelings, I personally think it’s a great idea.<br /><br />I love these people with all my heart. I accept all their flaws and will continue to love them unconditionally forever. Each of them knows the other so well it seems like the information is just naturally embedded in each of their subconcious. I swear, the amount of emotion this brings forth in me is perplexing. <br />Each relationship had a different basis, different feelings, and different personalities. But each relationship, no matter how they end or progress, open our eyes to their most appealing qualities, which inevitably leads to me either liking or even loving all of these people, each in their own unique way. I have grown impossibly fond of each of these people and I will cherish them till the end of time. <br /><br />In a lot of series we get to know more and more about the protagonist through the series but in this trilogy I feel like we’ve learnt most of the things about her in the first book and instead we’ve joined her in a journey of love and hope, and watched her grow. <br />There are life lessons here. It teaches you so much about family, friends, first love and so much more I can't begin to describe. This book wrung my heart dry. The reality and truth that comes along with this amazing story is something I will never forget. The friendship in this book is enough to make me want to keep reading them forever. <br /><br />If someone ever asks me what this trilogy about the only answer that will encompass this marvelous journey is <i>Love</i>. Love comes in many forms, I don't just mean the love interests I mean the family and the friends and everything that comes along with these life changing bonds. These relationships are the ones that shape our personality, they made us who we are today and those relationships are never to be underestimated. <br /><br />I shall never forget this trilogy and never once have I been disappointed by it. It will always remain one of my favorite contemporaries. I rate this book 5 stars just as I rated the previous two. <br /><br />I’ll always remember : <b>
  <i>”It all started with a love letter.”</i>
</b></span>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1846379209" />
    <a title="emma" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/32879029-emma"><img alt="emma" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1520568130p2/32879029.jpg" /></a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1846379209" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15109244945322210630">here is what i need:<br/>- netflix to adapt the other books in the To All the Boys I've Loved Before series<br/>- Kitty to get her own series IMMEDIATELY.<br/><br/>find other this-related opinions in my FULL REVIEW OF THIS WHOLE ASS SERIES, here: <a target='_blank' rel='noopener nofollow' href='https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/08/18/to-all-the-boys-ive-loved-before-series-review-the-emotional-rollercoaster-of-a-lifetime/'>https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br/><br/>------------<br/><br/>I can’t even tell you how much I wanted to love this book.<br/><br/>I reread To All the Boys I Loved Before in May of last year, and not liking it was the equivalent of when you bake cookies but something went wrong with the dough </span>
  <span id="freeText15109244945322210630" style="display:none">here is what i need:<br />- netflix to adapt the other books in the To All the Boys I've Loved Before series<br />- Kitty to get her own series IMMEDIATELY.<br /><br />find other this-related opinions in my FULL REVIEW OF THIS WHOLE ASS SERIES, here: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.com/2018/08/18/to-all-the-boys-ive-loved-before-series-review-the-emotional-rollercoaster-of-a-lifetime/">https://emmareadstoomuch.wordpress.co...</a><br /><br />------------<br /><br />I can’t even tell you how much I wanted to love this book.<br /><br />I reread To All the Boys I Loved Before in May of last year, and not liking it was the equivalent of when you bake cookies but something went wrong with the dough and they all run into one giant flat liquid-looking Thing with really unattractive chocolate chip lumps.<br /><br />In a word, DEVASTATING.<br /><br />I reallyreallyreally didn’t want to recreate that cookie-disaster level of sadness. Which is definitely why I didn’t read the second book until eight months later, and not because I’m a procrastinator who can’t stick to anything, or something ridiculous like that.<br /><br />To prevent myself from skipping out on this book, which was sure to be an injection straight to the veins of pure joy, I checked out both PS I Still Love You and this on Overdrive, thus giving myself a week to read both.<br /><br />Yes.<br /><br />I forced myself to read this book. I gave myself a time limit. I essentially school assigned reading’d this sh*t.<br /><br />And guess what?<br /><br />It worked.<br /><br />I don’t think I’ve ever actively wanted to like a book while reading it so much as I did with this. <br /><br />To All the Boys I’ve Loved Before helped me get back into reading. As I was emerging from my middle school dark ages of never reading (which were also the dark ages of Aeropostale graphic tees, fake Uggs, and bad haircuts), I used to find books in one way.<br /><br />This was by entering the Target young adult book aisle, reading every inside jacket or back cover, writing down the titles that seemed interesting, and requesting them from the library.<br /><br />They were mostly contemporaries, and this was one of them. I loved it. I stayed up until 2 a.m. reading it on a school night - I remember the experience distinctly.<br /><br />So hating it upon reread was just a goddamn nightmare. A nightmare compounded by PS I Still Love You, which I found to be even worse than its predecessor.<br /><br />But those actual night terrors only made me more determined to like this book.<br /><br />And then I realized something: at least a fraction (and a sizable fraction) of liking a book is the determination to like it. If I really wanted to like Always and Forever, Lara Jean, I was sure I could.<br /><br />So I did. And it worked.<br /><br />It still had a lot of the things I hated about the first two books. The high school drama; the saccharine, immature quality; above all, the existence of the character of Peter Kavinsky.<br /><br />There were even bits about this plotline that I hated. Mostly that it consisted of Peter being a completely unforgivable asshole and being forgiven somehow, and the fact that it kept referring to characters rarely mentioned as Lara Jean’s friends as if friendships could be willed into narrative being.<br /><br />Guess what? They can’t. I still know that Lara Jean only ever talks to her family, Peter, and the half-friends she had in the other books. So there.<br /><br />But also, I was <i>so sad</i> when this was over. I’m going to miss the way that Jenny Han writes this world. No one can write details like Jenny Han. The clothes, the rooms, the decorations, the craft projects, the Korean culture, the baked goods - oh god, the baked goods.<br /><br />And the character of Kitty (Lara Jean’s younger sister) is the great love of my life. I am mourning her, as I knew I would mourn her.<br /><br />I’m more surprised that I’m mourning this series too.<br /><br />Bottom line: I am endlessly impressed with myself for no good reason, and if there is a higher power or justice or love or anything good in this world, Jenny Han will give Kitty the series she deserves.<br /><br />------------<br />why am i crying in the club rn?<br /><br />in a twist no one saw coming, i actually liked this book.<br /><br />WHAT A THRILL.<br /><br />review to come<br /><br />------------<br />CURRENTLY-READING UPDATE<br /><br />on may 2, 2017, i expected to have a joyous reread of this series and dive delightedly into this book.<br /><br />on may 11, 2017, i was dealt the crushing blow that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/989214934?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener"> To All the Boys I've Loved Before is...not good.</a><br /><br />on january 26, 2018, i finally persevered, only to realize that <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1281232014?book_show_action=false&amp;from_review_page=1" rel="nofollow noopener">PS I Still Love You was somehow even worse.</a><br /><br />now, today, i will face the final boss.<br /><br />AND STILL I'M JUST HOPING THIS BOOK IS GOOD.</span>
  <a data-text-id="15109244945322210630" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1757599144" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1757599144" />
    <a title="C.G. Drews" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews"><img alt="C.G. Drews" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1521552918p2/11375137.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1757599144?book_show_action=true">Mar 22, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="C.G. Drews" class="user" itemprop="url" name="C.G. Drews" href="/user/show/11375137-c-g-drews">C.G. Drews</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=read-2018">read-2018</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=contemporary">contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/11375137-c-g-drews?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1757599144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3104540947719390591"><b>I really do love this trilogy a lot! It's just so warm and lovely.</b> This book is a complete Hufflepuff (also shout out to Lara Jean saying on page she was a 'Puff because yes. Yes, she is.) Buuut I didn't love it as much as the first one (or the second really) and I think this is because the only conflict was Lara Jean/Peter doing the "will they won't they" stay together. Which has been the conflict in EVERY book. So IDK?! I was just getting so stressed by this point. I really root for them! But </span>
  <span id="freeText3104540947719390591" style="display:none"><b>I really do love this trilogy a lot! It's just so warm and lovely.</b> This book is a complete Hufflepuff (also shout out to Lara Jean saying on page she was a 'Puff because yes. Yes, she is.) Buuut I didn't love it as much as the first one (or the second really) and I think this is because the only conflict was Lara Jean/Peter doing the "will they won't they" stay together. Which has been the conflict in EVERY book. So IDK?! I was just getting so stressed by this point. I really root for them! But after 3 books of "will they won't they" by the end of it all I just am feeling depleted. So ahhhh. I still love the trilogy <i>a lot</i> though.<br /><br /><b>Lara Jean is an adorable thing.</b> She just SO IS. And her character development is so Soft™ but actually quite visible by this book! Like she is a lot more confident. I just wiiiiish she communicated better. (Me @ every YA protagonist ever.) Some characters are here like "my life's work is to save the world" and Lara Jean is "my life's work is to find the perfect chocolate chip recipe" and I'm like SAME GIRL, SAME. Relatable content.<br /><br />Also Peter needs to stahp being so DARN ADORABLE. He is!! He is the cutest book boy ever (And he's a jock so like?!? Who am I.) I also like how he can be a jock + Lara Jean literally scrapbooks and bakes cookies all t he time and = they WORK TOGETHER. <b>I love for relationships that are so different yet fit so well!</b><br /><br /><b>I wasn't a biggest fan of her dad's wedding haha.</b> Mostly because I am not a big fan of weddings. I literally tried to melt into the sidewalk for my sisters'. I have been forced to attend FOUR SIBLINGS' WEDDINGS AND IT IS NOT OK. Why must everyone get married fffssss. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Also not the hugest fan of Trina? I just didn't relaly feel like I knew her. And Lara Jean is constantly like "oh they fit so well" but I never really saw it. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>And I just LIVE for all the cute moments!</b> Stargazing! Pancakes! Flower crowns! Baking scenes! Peter fake-pouting! Lara Jean fake-being-stern! KITTY BEING SO LETHALLY SHARP. Kitty is like here to give you grief and I live for it.<br /><br /><b>Soooo, spoiler moment.</b> Because I must: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I just feel, I guess, a little disappointed because I feel Peter loves Lara Jean waaaay more than she loves him. And I'm sad ok. Their like 3-day break up was dumb and just...ugh. I feel like the amount of times they've broken up and gotten back together makes me scared of them being A Thing forever. AND MAYBE I'M A DUMB SAPPY ROMANTIC BUT I WANT TO SHUT THIS BOOK AND THINK THEY'RE A THING FOREVER. They're adorable. sobsob I feel it has been a battle for 3 books to have them together and I jUST want to close this book and know they're not going to break up and be dumb ok?!???????? Peter's contract at the end THO. afdjaskld. I love them. One of my top ships. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br /><b>Okay but just remember I am a nasty heartless Slytherin and nO ONE CAN KNOW how much I love this sweet warm series that is like bread and sugar and cuddles.</b> Although book 1 is forever the best of the three. But I'm still in a state of satisfaction. I am a satisfied warm piece of bread. I am.</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1638014392" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2681592486599838120">"I guess that's part of growing up, too - saying goodbye to the things you used to love"<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444675117ra/16534167.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><b> GAH THE FEELS IN THIS BOOK ARE OVERWHELMING </b><br/>Lara Jean knows she loves Peter but when their future plans go awry and outside pressures seep in, will they be able to make it through? Or would it be best if they called it quits?<br/><br/>I was going to give this book 4.5/stars but decided on 5 because of how it made me think of it and feel days after finishing reading.<br/><br/>"I suppose I'll say it all started with a love lette</span>
  <span id="freeText2681592486599838120" style="display:none">"I guess that's part of growing up, too - saying goodbye to the things you used to love"<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1444675117ra/16534167.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><b> GAH THE FEELS IN THIS BOOK ARE OVERWHELMING </b><br>Lara Jean knows she loves Peter but when their future plans go awry and outside pressures seep in, will they be able to make it through? Or would it be best if they called it quits?<br><br>I was going to give this book 4.5/stars but decided on 5 because of how it made me think of it and feel days after finishing reading.<br><br>"I suppose I'll say it all started with a love letter"<br><br>Jenny Han writes a contemporary romance tale with realism rare in the YA world. I didn't know what to expect with this third instalment in the series but it definitely did not disappoint. I was really pleased with how much more development this story had. It is still the coming of age story you remember from the past books but it grows with the readers as well. This series will be in my heart. I recommend this series to any younglings looking for a story about young love, family and finding your place in the world. <br><br>***Sometimes in the book I was sort of annoyed or stressing for Lara Jean and her controlling tendencies as well as her avoidance of her problems, etc. After reading though I appreciated that Jenny Han wrote her character with such flaws because even though as a reader I was sometimes annoyed, I was able to see the realism behind the character. Lara Jean isn't perfect and has many flaws. Which is great to see because it's rare in YA books. I enjoyed seeing it in this book and hope to see more character flaws like this in the future<br><br>This was an amazing conclusion!! What did you guys think?</span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2524017779" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5419279419730629472"><b>
  <u>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED</u>
</b><br/><br/>I read a lot of series this year, but I don't think many had such a profound effect on me as this one did. When I started To All the Boys I've Loved Before, I expected it to be a fun and fluffy contemporary I would enjoy for it's cuteness and that would be about it. But this series turned out to be so much more for me and I always find the best books are the ones like that. Where they just surprise you by how much they end up meaning to you. I cannot believe how quickly</span>
  <span id="freeText5419279419730629472" style="display:none"><b>
  <u>FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED</u>
</b><br /><br />I read a lot of series this year, but I don't think many had such a profound effect on me as this one did. When I started To All the Boys I've Loved Before, I expected it to be a fun and fluffy contemporary I would enjoy for it's cuteness and that would be about it. But this series turned out to be so much more for me and I always find the best books are the ones like that. Where they just surprise you by how much they end up meaning to you. I cannot believe how quickly my whole entire heart fell in love with this series. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“One day all of this will be proof, proof that we were here, proof that we loved each other. It’s the guarantee that no matter what happens to us in the future, this time was ours.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />I had heard a lot of mixed reviews for Always and Forever, Lara Jean but I really liked it. Of all three, this felt like the most mature of the books. I loved that, as the books went on, the complexity of the issues Lara Jean and Peter face increases. Jenny Han really captures anxieties around growing up and how it feels to have to tackle these changes you feel are so enormous, and she writes about them so well. <b>I felt like this book was super realistic, and the trials Lara Jean and Peter face were super relatable</b>. I've always related to Lara Jean and her struggles but I think this (followed closely by P.S I Still Love You) most strongly resonated with me. <br /><br />Lara Jean was the perfect eyes to read this series through. I adore Lara Jean. She’s a hopeless romantic, a baking goddess and honestly, a little bit extra. But I really loved that about her. I related to her so much and I really liked how she developed as a character and person throughout this series. She becomes much more mature and confident and outspoken as the series progresses and I really loved watching that change. Her character development was very well written, and I like how we follow her as she accrues knowledge and wisdom from her friends and family and from within herself that she takes into the next book. Her character arc felt continuous, which is great, because I hate when it feels like each books starts the character growth all over again. <br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I don’t want to forget any of this. The way he’s looking at me at this very moment. How, when he kisses me, I still get shivers down my back, every time. I want to hold on to everything so tight.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br />Of course we have to talk about the ROMANCE. Peter and Lara Jean’s relationship is far from perfect. Han deconstructs Lara Jeans idealised vision of romance she’s picked up from novels and film and that creates a teenage romance that is realistic in it’s messiness and oftentimes immaturity. But I really, really loved their romance. Peter is sweet and funny and a bit of a jock but in a really loveable puppy way. Lara Jean is so dorky and awkward but she’s also so so sweet too and the scenes of them together literally killed me from the cute fluffiness of it all. The truth is I’d date them both in a heartbeat. I also love how sex positive this was and how Lara Jean and Peter’s first time attempting to have sex was handled.<br /><br />But it was the relationship between the Song Sisters that was my favourite aspect of this book (and series). I loved every single song sister individually. Kitty was probably my favourite but I adored Margot too. The sister relationship was honestly so spot on, and I related to it a lot as a middle sister of three girls. Seeing three sisters in books is so rare, this is one of the few series I’ve seen do it and the only one I’ve seen do it so very well. Hen nailed the complexities and intricacies of navigating relationships with your sisters. Theres ups and downs but ultimately you always have eachothers backs. This was perfectly communicated here and I felt incredibly seen through reading Lara Jean’s relationship with her sisters.<br /><br /><i>
  <blockquote>“I have a feeling that when I'm Stormy's age, these everyday moments will be what I remember: Peter's head bent, biting into a chocolate chip cookie; the sun coming through the cafeteria window, bouncing off his brown hair; him looking at me.” </blockquote>
</i><br /><br /><b>In conclusion:</b> I love everything about these books and since there is no more coming out all I can do is: eat chocolate chip cookies, while rereading the books and crying about how long it'll be until P.S I Still Love You drops on netflix.<br /><br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="5419279419730629472" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer1856773118156700590"><br/>I never imagined falling for a too handsome, too popular jock but Peter is just too adorable to resist. Gaaaah! adsfghjklmnopqwertqwerty! He’s basically the reason why I liked the conclusion to this trilogy so much. All of my favorite moments in this finale involve him:<br/><br/>1. Learning from Kitty how to braid <b>*just adorable*</b><br/>2. Using every chance he gets to practice braiding Lara Jean’s hair<br/>3. His bachelor’s party for Lara Jean’s Dad<br/>4.   <span id="freeText1856773118156700590" style="display:none"><br />I never imagined falling for a too handsome, too popular jock but Peter is just too adorable to resist. Gaaaah! adsfghjklmnopqwertqwerty! He’s basically the reason why I liked the conclusion to this trilogy so much. All of my favorite moments in this finale involve him:<br /><br />1. Learning from Kitty how to braid <b>*just adorable*</b><br />2. Using every chance he gets to practice braiding Lara Jean’s hair<br />3. His bachelor’s party for Lara Jean’s Dad<br />4. The way he looks at Lara Jean <b>*sighs*</b><br />5. How he always compliments the best way he can Lara Jean’s baked goods <br />6. Peter always trying to win Lara Jean’s dad and sisters <b>*I think that’s the sweetest*</b><br />7. Peter in a tux <b>*heart eyes*</b><br />8. Peter picking their theme song during prom <b>*oh, my heart!*</b><br />9. His birthday surprise for Lara Jean <b>*I’m a goner*</b><br />10. Peter thinking he isn’t good enough for Lara Jean. <b>*Awww!*</b><br />11. His message on Lara Jean’s yearbook <b>*Peter, I’m yours!* (Nobody tells my husband, alright?) </b><br /><br />I have developed this unrelenting loyalty for <b>Peter</b> so much that every time <b>John Ambrose</b> enters the picture, I practically yell at him to get the heck out. Lol. But Peter aside, I think this finale is the perfect conclusion to the trilogy. I love seeing the growth of each of the characters in the story (even Genevieve) but especially <b>Lara Jean.</b> What I love about Lara Jean is her kind and forgiving heart. I like that she doesn’t try to complicate things and how she’s often reasonable. I love her connection with each of the person she loves, with her sisters, her dad and Peter. What you see is what you get, as they say. I do not doubt I’ll read these books again in the near future. Lol.</span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer16139454140854493205"><b>5 Stars!</b><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Is this how it goes? You fall in love, and nothing seems truly scary anymore, and life is one big possibility?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br/><br/>I CANNOT CONTAIN MY FEELS!<br/><br/>*swoons uncontrollably<br/><br/>This conclusion of <i>To All the Boys I've Loved Before</i> trilogy was truly superb. It's THE PERFECT ending that I've been looking for. I hated Peter Kavinsky in <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20698530.P_S__I_Still_Love_You__To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before___2_' title='P.S. I Still Love You (To All the Boys I've Loved Before, #2) by Jenny Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>P.S. I Still Love You</a> but this book took all my rage away. Why? Because <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han' title='Jenny Han' rel='nofollow noopener'>Jenny Han</a> redeemed his character and it was all it took to make me swoon over him again.<br/><br/>I r</span>
  <span id="freeText16139454140854493205" style="display:none"><b>5 Stars!</b><br><br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Is this how it goes? You fall in love, and nothing seems truly scary anymore, and life is one big possibility?”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br><br>I CANNOT CONTAIN MY FEELS!<br><br>*swoons uncontrollably<br><br>This conclusion of <i>To All the Boys I've Loved Before</i> trilogy was truly superb. It's THE PERFECT ending that I've been looking for. I hated Peter Kavinsky in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/20698530.P_S__I_Still_Love_You__To_All_the_Boys_I_ve_Loved_Before___2_" title="P.S. I Still Love You (To All the Boys I've Loved Before, #2) by Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">P.S. I Still Love You</a> but this book took all my rage away. Why? Because <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/151371.Jenny_Han" title="Jenny Han" rel="nofollow noopener">Jenny Han</a> redeemed his character and it was all it took to make me swoon over him again.<br><br>I rarely enjoy YA these days so I was glad to find myself really loving this book from start to finish. As a matter of fact, this book is my favorite out of all the books in this series. I loved the drama that was not overdone, the romance which was totally cute, and Lara Jean's relationship with her family.<br><br>I had a lot of favorite scenes, for sure (Lara Jean's birthday, Dr. Covey and Trina's practice dance, the double date, ahh so much more!) and if only I could paint them in my memory to last forever, I would. *sigh And the soundtracks.. OMG! Did I just read Shania Twain lyrics out there? I loveeeeee!<br><br><b>Favorite characters of all time: KITTY and CHRIS.</b><br><br>After finishing the book, I felt like I was floating in a sea of clouds. It was such a sweet ending. I loved Peter and Lara Jean's journey and I can't help but start to miss everything that happened between them. You can only imagine how I became elated and at the same time, quite sad that their story already ended. It was totally a lovely conclusion. So worth it! I don't think I would ever forget this sweet piece of a chocolate chipsy story. Enough said because I'm crying with feels. *cries<br><br><blockquote>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('dsridrXPuvkuGX8EuK9vFPpwqBEFqsTQzGOI+46BJyuapbpzgK+diIk1FCdYPBZngbEbZiRx2G+t5Go3msLHIA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nJLh+NN9UdMCkZPxqqxTK7OMV6yhWlIeOxtTlwkwa0Zw/bn95h12oqW9+NJKPypYyE3k24CBTqFanLFbHXOLTQ==')})
  }
//]]>

      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_39939417'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/39939417-five-feet-apart?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">Five Feet Apart<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17977608.Rachael_Lippincott?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Rachael Lippincott<\/a><span title=\"Goodreads Author!\">*<\/span>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.19 avg rating &mdash; 85,225 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 2018\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer5736312516753375431\">In this moving story two teens fall in love with just one minor complication—they can’t get within five feet of each other without risking their lives.\n\nCan you love someone you can never touch?\n\nStella Grant likes to be in control—even though her to<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText5736312516753375431\" style=\"display:none\">In this moving story two teens fall in love with just one minor complication—they can’t get within five feet of each other without risking their lives.\n\nCan you love someone you can never touch?\n\nStella Grant likes to be in control—even though her totally out of control lungs have sent her in and out of the hospital most of her life. At this point, what Stella needs to control most is keeping herself away from anyone or anything that might pass along an infection and jeopardize the possibility of a lung transplant. Six feet apart. No exceptions.\n\nThe only thing Will Newman wants to be in control of is getting out of this hospital. He couldn’t care less about his treatments, or a fancy new clinical drug trial. Soon, he’ll turn eighteen and then he’ll be able to unplug all these machines and actually go see the world, not just its hospitals.\n\nWill’s exactly what Stella needs to stay away from. If he so much as breathes on Stella she could lose her spot on the transplant list. Either one of them could die. The only way to stay alive is to stay apart. But suddenly six feet doesn’t feel like safety. It feels like punishment.\n\nWhat if they could steal back just a little bit of the space their broken lungs have stolen from them? Would five feet apart really be so dangerous if it stops their hearts from breaking too?<\/span>\n  <a data-text-id=\"5736312516753375431\" href=\"#\" onclick=\"swapContent(\$(this));; return
